The Language of Kʘxĩǂˀibian

Natively known as: Kʘxĩǂˀib /kʘxĩˈǂˀib/

...and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind...
ʘxō ī ǃqikǂ kǁxãkǃ ū ǁoyt ʘxō aduǂ ū īǁˀ ǁʼikǂx ku ǀxīǃq
Pronunciation: /ʘχoː iː ǃqikǂ kǁxãkǃ uː ǁojt ʘχoː aˈduǂ uː iːǁˀ ǁʼikǂx ku ǀχiːǃq/
Kʘxĩǂˀibian word order: and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind

Phonological rules (in order of application):

  • m → n / _#
  • h → Ø / V_
  • g → h / V_V
  • k → ʔ / _#
  • h → j / _E
  • e → æ / _P

Grammar

Main word order: Subject-Verb-Object-Oblique. "Mary opened the door with a key" turns into Mary opened the door with a key.
Adjective order: Adjectives are positioned before the noun.
Adposition: prepositions

Noun

Singular No affix
ǃongǀõǂ /ǃoŋˈǀõǂ/

Verbs

Past tense may be indicated with the word:

Past particle u /u/
past tense particle

Future If starts with vowel: Prefix n-
Else: Prefix niː-
nīǁʢaʘˀ /ˈniːǁʢaʘˀ/

Imperfective aspect

The ‘imperfective’ aspect refers to ongoing actions, such as I am studying,
and habitual actions, such as I study (every night).

It is indicated with the word:

Imperfect particle ēkǀx /eːkǀx/
imperfect particle

Derivational morphology

Adjective → noun = If starts with vowel: Prefix aǂ-
Else: Prefix aǂẽ-
Noun → adjective = Prefix ǁχaː-
Noun → verb = If starts with vowel: Prefix ikn-
Else: Prefix iknu-
Verb → noun = If starts with vowel: Prefix õnh-
Else: Prefix õnhi-
Verb → adjective = Prefix o-
Adjective → verb = Prefix kǂxiː-
Adjective → adverb = Prefix õ-
One who Xs (e.g. paint → painter) = If starts with vowel: Prefix õgm-
Else: Prefix õgmo-
Place of (e.g. wine → winery) = If starts with vowel: Prefix ǀ-
Else: Prefix ǀu-
Diminutive = If starts with vowel: Prefix ũʘ-
Else: Prefix ũʘaː-
Augmentative = If starts with vowel: Prefix aːǀχ-
Else: Prefix aːǀχaː-
